Merging Penalties (Tadakhul) When a Hand Is Cut Then the Victim Killed
Intra-Hanafi dispute on merging penalties for multiple injuries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on tadakhul (merging) of multiple penalties and apply it to distinguish when multiple intentional injuries trigger separate qisas versus a single penalty.

Core Idea
Intentional acts never merge; only two errors without healing merge into one diyah.

The chapter moves from single injuries to multiple injuries. A key scenario: a person cuts off another's hand and then kills him. The question is whether the two penalties merge. The general rule is that penalties do not merge except in the case of two unintentional (khata') acts without healing in between. For intentional acts, there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement. This passage presents the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and his two companions, exploring the principles of equivalence in qisas and the effect of healing (bur'). Understanding this will sharpen your ability to analyze multiple injuries in qisas cases.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule of tadakhul
From the passage, identify the four scenarios (both intentional, different types, both errors with healing, both errors without healing) and determine which merge. The rule: only both errors without healing merge.
The exception is only for two errors (khata'an) with no healing between.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Find where the text says 'This is the statement of Abu Hanifa' and 'According to the two companions they merge'. Identify the specific issue: for two intentional injuries, do they merge?
Abu Hanifa says no merger; Sahibayn say merger because acts are homogeneous and no healing.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Examine the reasoning: qisas requires equivalence in form and meaning (mumathalah surawan wa ma'nan). Cutting the hand must be repaid by cutting; killing by killing. Combining both is possible, so both must be executed. Also, if two people had each committed one act, each would owe qisas; same for one person.
Key point: equivalence in both form and meaning is required; reducing to only killing loses formal equivalence.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
They argue it is like two errors: the acts are homogeneous (both intentional injuries causing death), no healing intervened, so they should merge. Also, combining wounds is obligatory when possible to avoid hardship.
They analogize to errors because both are injuries leading to death, and consider the hand die with the body, so only one penalty suffices.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa: the offender's hand is cut first, then he is executed. Under Sahibayn: only execution is carried out (the hand cut is absorbed). Also, the guardian (wali) has a choice under Abu Hanifa: either order both or only execution (but that sacrifices formal equivalence).
The difference is whether the hand is amputated before execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : لما فرغ من ذكر حكم الجناية الواحدة شرع في ذكر الجنايات المتعددة لأن الاثنين ثم قتله أخذ بالأمرين ولو عمدين أو مختلفين أو خطئين تخلل بينهما برء أو لا إلا في خطئين لم يتخلل بينهما برء فتجب دية واحدة كمن ضرب رجلاً مائة سوط فبرئ من تسعين ومات من عشرة فإن عفا المقطوع عن القطع فمات ضمن القاطع الدية ولو عفا بعد الواحد . قال رحمه الله : (ومن قطع يد رجل ثم قتله أخذ بالأمرين ولو عمدين أو مختلفين أو خطئين تخلل بينهما برء أو لا إلا في خطئين لم يتخلل بينهما برء فتجب دية واحدة كمن ضرب رجلاً مائة سوط فبرئ من تسعين ومات من عشرة يعني إذا قطع يده ثم قتله يجب عليه موجب القطع وموجب القتل إن كانا عمدين أو أحدهما عمد والآخر خطأ أو كانا خطئين وتخلل بينهما برء وفي خطئين لم يتخلل بينهما برء فتجب عليه دية واحدة، فحاصله أن الكل لا يتداخل إلا في خطئين فإنهما يتداخلان فيجب فيهما دية واحدة، إذا لم يتخلل بينهما برء، وإن تخلل بينهما برء لا يتداخلان. أما الأول وهو ما إذا كانا عمدين فالمذكور قول أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يتداخلان فيقتل حداً ولا يقطع يده لأن الجمع بينهما ممكن لتجانس الفعلين وعدم تخلل البرء بينهما فصار كالخطاين، وهذا لأن الجمع بين الجراحات واجب ما أمكن لأن القتل يقع بضربات غالباً واعتبار كل ضربة على حدتها يؤدي إلى الحرج فيجمع تيسيراً إلا أن لا يمكن بأن يختلف حكم الفعلين كالعمد والخطأ أو يتخلل البرء بينهما لأن البرء قاطع للسراية فلا يمكن أن يجعل الثاني تتميماً للأول فيعتبر على حاله وأمكن ذلك قبل البرء فصار كسراية الأول. وله أن الجمع متعذر لأن حز الرقبة يمنع سراية القطع كالبرء حتى لو صدر من شخصين وجب على كل واحد منهما القصاص فكذا إذا كان من شخص واحد فتقطع أولاً يده ثم يقتلوه إن شاؤوا وإن شاؤوا قتلوه من غير قطع لأن القصاص يعتمد المساواة في الفعل وذلك بأن يكون القتل بالقتل والقطع بالقطع واستيفاء القطع بالقتل متعذر لاختلافهما حقيقة وحكماً، ولأن المماثلة صورة ومعنى يكون باستيفائهما وبالاكتفاء بالقتل لم توجد المماثلة إلا معنى فلا يصار إليه مع القدرة على المماثلة صورة ومعنى فيخير الولي بخلاف ما إذا مات من السراية لأن الفعل واحد وبخلاف ما إذا كان خطأين لأن الموجب فيه الدية وهو بدل المحل والمقتول واحد ألا ترى أن عشرة لو قتلوا واحداً خطأ يجب عليهم دية واحدة لاتحاد المحل وإن تعدد الفعل، ولو قتلوه به جميعاً لأن القصاص جزاء الفعل وهو متعدد وإن اتحد، ولأن أرش اليد لو وجب كان يجب عليه عند الجزاء لأنه وقت استحكام أثر الفعل ولا سبيل إليه لأنه حينئذ تجب دية النفس بالجزاء فيجتمع وجوب بدل الجزاء والكل في حالة واحدة وهو محال، ولو وجب ذلك لوجب بقتل النفس الواحد ديات كثيرة للأطراف لأنها تتلف بتلف النفس، أما القتل والقطع فقصاصان فأمكن اجتماعهما، وبخلاف ما إذا قطع وسرى حيث يكتفي بالقطع لاتحاد الفعل . وأما الثاني وهو ما إذا كانا مختلفين بأن كان أحدهما خطأ والآخر عمداً والثالث وهو ما إذا كانا خطأين وتحلل بينما برء فلأن الجمع
Section: When he finished mentioning the ruling of a single injury, he began to mention multiple injuries because two (or more) then he killed, he is taken with both (penalties), whether both are intentional, or different, or both are errors, whether healing intervened between them or not, except in two errors where healing did not intervene, then one diyah is obligatory like one who hits a man with one hundred lashes: he healed from ninety and died from ten. If the one whose hand was cut forgives the cutting then he dies, the cutter is liable for diyah, even if he forgave after the one (act). He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Whoever cuts the hand of a man then kills him, he is taken with both (penalties), whether both are intentional or different or both errors, whether healing intervened or not, except in two errors where healing did not intervene, then one diyah is obligatory, like one who hits a man with one hundred lashes: he healed from ninety and died from ten. Meaning, if he cuts his hand then kills him, he owes the liability for the cutting and the liability for the killing if both are intentional, or one intentional and the other error, or both errors with healing intervening, and in two errors without healing intervening, he owes one diyah. The sum is that the penalties do not merge except in two errors where they merge, thus one diyah is owed, if healing did not intervene; if healing did intervene, they do not merge. As for the first case, where both are intentional, that is the statement of Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), they merge (in that case) and he is executed as a hadd punishment and his hand is not cut, because combining them is possible due to the homogeneity of the two acts and the absence of healing between them, so it becomes like the case of two errors. This is because combining wounds is obligatory as much as possible, since killing usually occurs with blows, and considering each blow separately leads to hardship, so they are combined for ease, except when impossible, such as when the legal ruling of the two acts differs (like intentional and error) or when healing intervenes, because healing cuts off the effect, so the second cannot be made a completion of the first, so each is considered separately, and it was possible before healing, so it becomes like the first's continued effect. And for him (Abu Hanifa) combining is impossible because cutting the neck prevents the effect of the cutting from reaching the hand, like healing; so if it came from two persons, each would owe qisas, so too if from one person. So they cut off his hand first, then kill him if they wish, or they kill him without cutting, because qisas depends on equivalence in the act, which means killing for killing and cutting for cutting, and executing cutting by killing is impossible due to difference in reality and legal status. And because equivalence in form and meaning is achieved by executing both, and by limiting to killing, equivalence is only in meaning, so it is not resorted to when there is ability for equivalence in form and meaning, so the guardian has a choice. Unlike if he dies from the effect (of the cut), because the act is one. And unlike if both are errors, because the liability is diyah which is substitution for the subject, and the killed one is one. Do you not see that if ten people kill one person by error, they owe one diyah due to the unity of the subject, even if the acts are multiple? And if they kill him all together (intentionally), each owes qisas because qisas is the recompense for the act, which is multiple even if the subject is one. And because if the arsh (compensation) for the hand were obligatory, it would be due at the time of execution (qisas) because it is the time of complete effect, and there is no way to it, because then the diyah for life would be due due to execution, so the obligation of substitution for a limb and the whole would be combined in one state, which is impossible. And if that were obligatory, then by killing one person many diyahs for limbs would become obligatory because they perish with the perishing of the life. As for killing and cutting, they are two qisas, so combining them is possible. And unlike the case where he cuts and the wound causes death, where he suffices with the cutting due to the unity of the act. As for the second case, where the two acts are different, one being error and the other intentional, and the third case where both are errors and healing intervened between them, then (the ruling is) because then...
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute from the chapter on qisas regarding multiple injuries committed by the same person. The passage deals with a scenario: a person first cuts off another's hand, then kills him. The question is whether the penalties for both acts merge or remain separate. The general rule: if both acts are intentional, or different (one intentional one error), or both errors with healing between, both penalties apply. The only exception is when both acts are errors (khata') without healing in between; then only one diyah is due (the penalties merge). Within the case of two intentional acts, there is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifa says both penalties apply: the hand must be cut first, then the killer executed. The Sahibayn say the penalties merge: the killer is executed as a fixed punishment (hadd) and the hand is not cut, because the acts are homogenous and no healing intervened, so it is like the case of two errors (where merging is allowed). The commentary then provides extensive reasoning for both views, including analogies to multiple blows from one or multiple persons, and the principle that qisas requires exact equivalence in form and meaning. The passage also discusses the effect of healing (bur') as cutting off the causal link, and the principle of 'ta'addud al-athar' (multiplicity of effects). The text ends mid-sentence discussing the case of different types of offenses.

Key Terms
التداخل (al-tadakhul): Legal merging of multiple penalties into one when multiple acts occur on the same subject.
البرء (al-bur'): Healing of the wound between injuries; it breaks the causal chain and prevents merger.
المماثلة صورة ومعنى (al-mumathalah surawan wa ma'nan): Equivalence in both form and meaning; a requirement for qisas that the retaliation exactly matches the injury in type and nature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which scenario do penalties for multiple injuries merge?
A) When both injuries are intentional and no healing occurs.
B) When both injuries are errors (khata') and no healing occurs.
C) When one injury is intentional and the other is error.
D) When both injuries are intentional and healing occurs.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, penalties for multiple injuries do not merge unless both are errors (khata') with no healing, but for intentional acts, each act requires its own qisas or compensation, as maintained by Abu Hanifa.

When Qisas Becomes Impossible: The Transformation to Diyah
Explains rule when qisas becomes impossible and diyah is due

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that diyah replaces qisas when impossibility arises from the culprit's side and distinguish the application of istihsan from qiyas in the confession scenario.

Core Idea
If qisas is impossible due to the culprit's action, the right turns to diyah — istihsan overrides qiyas to prevent blood waste.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we examine a core principle of Hanafi criminal law: when retaliation (qisas) becomes impossible due to a cause originating from the offender, the right to retribution transforms into a financial claim (diyah). The commentator presents the general rule, then applies it to a contested scenario where a killer confesses to accident but the guardian claims intent. Here, the Hanafi school uses istihsan to depart from strict analogy, ensuring the victim's blood is not wasted.

Guided Path
1
State the General Hanafi Rule
Extract the principle: when execution of qisas is prevented due to a cause from the culprit's side, the right is not abandoned but transforms into diyah (blood money).
The maxim: 'من قبله' (from his side) is key.
2
Identify the Disputed Scenario
Focus on the case: killer confesses to accidental killing, guardian claims intentional. Both agree on the fact of killing but differ on degree.
This is where Zufar differs from the mainstream Hanafi view.
3
Analyze Zufar's Qiyas Argument
Zufar analogizes to the case where killer confesses to intentional and guardian claims accident: in that case, nothing is due. He argues that the confession is contradicted by the guardian's claim, so it is as if no confession exists.
Qiyas leads to no liability.
4
Understand the Hanafi Istihsan Argument
The Hanafi response distinguishes the two cases: in Zufar's analogy, the prevention of qisas comes from the guardian (who claims accident), so no diyah. Here, the prevention comes from the killer himself (by claiming mistake), so diyah is owed to protect the victim's blood.
Istihsan considers the source of impossibility.
5
Recognize the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical outcome: if killer confesses to accident and guardian claims intentional → Hanafi says diyah, Zufar says nothing. If killer confesses to intentional and guardian claims accident → both say nothing (but for different reasons).
The difference matters for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنايات باب القصاص فيما دون النفس عن القطع وما يحدث منه أو عن الجناية لا فالخطأ من الثلث والعمد من كل المال وإن وهو الخطأ، فإذا تعذر صيانة الاستيفاء القصاص من قبل من له الحق لا يصار إلى المال لأن الشرع غير حقه في القصاص لكن هو الذي فوته وفرط بإتيان ما أعجزه فأهدره فلم يبق مستحقاً للنظر، وإذا أقر القاتل بالخطأ وادعى الولي العمد لم يقتص ولزمه الدية استحساناً. وقال زفر : لا يلزمه شيء قياساً لأن ما أقربه لم يثبت لأنه كذبه المدعي في إقراره بمقتضي دعواه القصاص وصار كما لو أقر القاتل بالعمد وادعى الولي الخطأ لا يلزمه شيء . هذا. ولنا أنهما تصادقا على القتل إلا أنه تعذر استيفاء القصاص بمعنى من الجناية قال: يقتص من المقر لأنهما تصادقا على وجوب القود ولو لم تتمكن الشبهة فيه حين أنكر الآخر الجناية لأنه يمكن الشبهة إنما يكون باختلاط الموجب وغير الموجب في المحل وذلك لا يتصور قبل وجوب الجناية من الآخر. وإذا ادعى الولي الخطأ فلا شيء على المقر لأنه لما أنكر الآخر الجناية صار كالعدم فبطل دعواه الخطأ، وإقرار القاتل بالعمد في هذا لا يجب شيء. وإن مات رجل من قطع يده ورجله فقال رجل قطعت يده عمداً وقال قطع عمرو رجله عمداً فقال الولي بل أنت قطعتهما يجب القصاص عليه لأنهما تصادقا عل وجوب القصاص والشركة لم تثبت لعدم دعواه، فإن قال الولي لا أدري من قطع رجله فلا شيء على قاطع اليد لأن قاطع الرجل مجهول يجز أن يكون خاطئاً أو صبياً أو مجنوناً فتعذر إيجاب القصاص، وتعذر استيفاء القصاص جاء من قبل من له الحق فإن جهل قاطع الرجل جهل قاطع اليد فلا يجب المال. ولو قال الولي بعد ذلك فلان قطع رجله عمداً وأنكر Book of offences, chapter of retaliation for less than life: regarding amputation and what results from it, or regarding the injury, no: so for mistake from one-third and for intentional from all wealth, and it is the mistake. So when execution of retaliation is prevented from the side of the one who has the right, one does not resort to wealth because the Law changed his right to retaliation, but he is the one who forfeited and transgressed by doing what incapacitated him, so he is disregarded and no longer deserving of consideration. And if the killer confesses to mistake and the guardian claims intentional, he is not retaliated against and diyah is incumbent on him by istihsan. Zufar said: nothing is incumbent on him by qiyas because what he confessed to is not established since the claimant denied his confession by virtue of his claim of retaliation, and it is like if the killer confessed to intentional and the guardian claimed mistake: nothing is incumbent on him. That is it. And we argue: they both agreed on the killing except that execution of retaliation was prevented due to a meaning from the killer's side, which is his claim of mistake, so diyah is obligatory to protect his blood from being wasted. And because in the guardian's view, retaliation is obligatory, but when he confessed to mistake, he confessed to wealth, and the guardian may leave retaliation and take wealth, and he did not explicitly state that, so he may take the wealth. And if he confessed to intentional and the guardian claimed mistake, his right is nullified because the prevention of execution of retaliation came from the side of the one who has the right. And if the guardian claimed intentional against two men, and one of them said: I cut his hand intentionally and this other cut his leg intentionally, and the other denied the injury, he said: retaliation is exacted from the confessor because they both agreed on the obligation of qisas, even if doubt did not arise therein when the other denied the injury, because doubt can only occur by mixing the obligatory and non-obligatory in the same locus, and that is inconceivable before the obligation of the injury from the other. And if the guardian claimed mistake, then nothing is on the confessor because when the other denied the injury, he became non-existent, so his claim of mistake is nullified. And the killer's confession of intentional in this does not require anything. And if a man died from amputation of his hand and leg, and a man said: I cut his hand intentionally, and another said: Amr cut his leg intentionally, and the guardian said: rather you cut both, retaliation is obligatory on him because they both agreed on the obligation of retaliation, and partnership is not established due to lack of his claim. And if the guardian said: I do not know who cut his leg, then nothing is on the cutter of the hand because the cutter of the leg is unknown, possibly being mistaken, a child, or insane, so making retaliation obligatory becomes impossible, and prevention of execution of retaliation came from the side of the one who has the right. And if the guardian later said: so-and-so cut his leg intentionally, and so-and-so denied, he does not have the right to kill the confessor by qiyas, but he has the right to kill him by istihsan because a child does not know his father's killer when there are many of them, so inconsistency is excused. And the author expressed with 'man' which is singular in form but plural in meaning because there is no difference in the ruling whether the doer is singular or plural.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, commenting on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses the general rule that when the execution of qisas (retaliation) becomes impossible due to a cause originating from the culprit, the right transforms into diyah (blood money). The sharh then provides several detailed scenarios: (1) If a killer confesses to accidental killing but the guardian claims intentional, Zufar argues by qiyas that nothing is due because the confession is unverified. The Hanafi position (istihsan) holds that both agree on the killing, but qisas is prevented by the killer's claim, so diyah is owed to prevent blood waste. (2) If one of two accused confesses and the other denies, retaliation is exacted from the confessor alone because the denial of the other prevents doubt (shubha). (3) If both confess to separate injuries causing death, and the guardian says one person did both, retaliation is on that person. (4) If the identity of one cutter is unknown, no liability falls on the known cutter because the impossibility of execution comes from the guardian's side (lack of knowledge). (5) If the guardian later identifies the second cutter, he may execute the confessor by istihsan, not by qiyas. The passage concludes with a grammatical note that the author's use of 'man' (who) in singular form encompasses multiple doers.

Key Terms
القصاص (al-Qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional homicide or injury, specifically here for injuries below life (like amputation).
الدية (al-Diyah): Blood money payable to the victim's heirs when qisas is not possible or is waived.
الاستحسان (al-Istihsan): A method of reasoning that favors a ruling based on departure from strict analogy (qiyas) due to a stronger evidence or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a killer confesses to accidental killing but the guardian claims intentional, what is the ruling?
A) No qisas and no diyah because the confession is unverified
B) Qisas is executed because the guardian's claim prevails
C) No qisas, but diyah is due by istihsan
D) The killer must take an oath

Key Takeaway
When qisas becomes impossible due to the culprit's own action (e.g., confessing to a lesser degree), the right transforms into diyah — an application of istihsan that protects the victim's blood.

Forgiveness of Retaliation and Its Effect on Diyah: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Covers the scenario where the victim forgives the amputation then dies, and the ruling on diyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the effect of limited forgiveness (e.g., 'I forgive you the cutting') on diyah when the victim dies, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Forgiveness limited to the act may still require diyah upon death according to Abu Hanifa's istihsan.

When a victim forgives only the specific act of injury (e.g., cutting) without mentioning consequences, and then dies from that injury, does the diyah become due? The Hanafi school has a well-known internal dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the forgiveness is void for death-related consequences and diyah is due by istihsan, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold the forgiveness valid and no diyah. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and identifies the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and forgiveness wording
The scenario involves intentional amputation or head wound. The victim forgives the 'cutting' (al-qat') or 'gash' (al-shajjah) but does not mention 'and what arises from it.' This limited wording is the crux of the dispute.
Forgiveness of 'the injury' (al-jinaayah) makes the culprit free from both qisas and diyah by consensus.
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa: The forgiveness of the cutting alone does not waive liability for death, because the death is a separate consequence that was not explicitly forgiven. The forgiveness of the cutting is void with respect to death, so retaliation is due, but he applies istihsan to substitute diyah from the culprit's wealth to avoid blood waste.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here because the victim's heirs would otherwise receive nothing.
3
Apply the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: The forgiveness of the cutting is clear and effective; it covers all consequences inherent in the act, including death. Therefore no diyah is due, and the culprit is fully free.
They argue that the victim's intention was to forgive the entire harmful act, not to reserve claims for hidden future events.
4
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the victim dies after forgiving only the cutting, Abu Hanifa requires diyah from the culprit's wealth; the Sahibayn require nothing. This difference directly impacts the financial liability of the offender.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., in al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya) adopt the view of the Sahibayn as the relied-upon position, because it is more lenient and avoids imposing additional financial burden after forgiveness.
The passage in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the dispute without explicit tarjih, but the trend in later fatwa is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
05 كتاب الجنايات باب القصاص فيما دون النفس حتى بإطلاقه قول الإمام. وفي الجامع الصغير : رجل قطع يد رجل ظلماً عمداً فعفا المقطوع يده عن القطع ثم سرى إلى النفس ومات أو شج إنسان موضحة عمداً فعفا المشجوج رأسه عن الشجة ثم سرى إلى النفس ومات يجب أن يعلم بأن هنا مسألتين: أحدهما في العمد والأخرى في الخطأ. وكل مسألة على وجوه : إما أن يقول المقطوعة يده عفوتك عن الجناية أو يقول عفوتك عن القطع وما يحدث منه فإن كانت الجناية عمداً فقال المقطوعة يده أو قال المشجوجة رأسه عفوتك عن الجناية صح العفو وبرئ من القطع أو الشجة أو مات لا يجب شيء في الحالين ثم تصح البراءة عن جميع المال، سواء برأ أو مات. وإن قال عفوتك عن القطع ولم يقل وما يحدث من القطع أو قال عفوتك عن الشجة ولم يقل وما يحدث منها صح العفو عندهم جميعاً، فلو مات تجب الدية. قال أبو حنيفة : مع أن العفو باطل والقصاص أن يجب على المعفو عنه القصاص إلا أني أستحسن وجوب الدية في ماله. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد بأن العفو عنه جائز ولا شيء على المعفو عنه لا القصاص ولا الدية. وهذا الذي ذكرنا إذا كانت الجناية عمداً، فإذا كانت خطأ إن عفا عن الجناية أو عن القطع وما يحدث منه صح العفو سواء برئ أو مات إلا أنه إن عفا في حال يخرج ويجيء ويذهب بعد الجناية وأنه على قول بعض المشايخ يعتبر من جميع ماله. وذكر في المنتقى في هذه الصورة أنه يعتبر من ثلث المال وإن عفا عن القطع إن اقتصر عن القطع إن برأ صح العفو بلا خلاف من جميع المال وإن صار قاتلاً فعلى قول أبي حنيفة العفو باطل وكان على عاقلة القاتل الدية، وعندهما العفو جائز كما لو عفا عن القطع وعما يحدث منه إلا إنه إن في حالة حكم الصحة بأن كان يذهب ويجيء يصح من جميع المال، وعلى قياس رواية المنتقى من ثلث المال، وإن عفا في حال حكم المرض بأن صار صاحب فراش يعتبر من ثلث المال. ولو قال عفوت عن الجناية أو عن القاطع وما يحدث منه كان عفواً عند دية النفس بالإجماع حتى إذا مات سقط كل الدية فيه غير أنه موجبه المال وقد تعلق به حق الورثة فيعتبر من الثلث كسائر أمواله بخلاف ما إذا كان المال لأن عمداً حيث يصح من جميع موجبه القصاص ولم يتعلق بحق الورثة لأنه ليس بمال. قال في العناية : فيه بحث وهو أن القصاص موروث بالاتفاق فكيف لم يتعلق به حق الورثة ثم قال : والجواب عنه أن المصنف نفي تعلق حق الورثة به لا كونه موروثاً ولا تنافي بينهما لأن حق الورثة إنما يثبت بطريق الخلافة وحكم الخلف لا يثبت مع وجود الأصل والقياس في المال أيضاً أن لا يثبت فيه تعلق حق الورثة إلا بعد موت المورث لكن ثبت ذلك شرعاً بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لأن تدع ورثتك أغنياء خير من تدعهم عالة يتكففون الناس وتركهم أغنياء إنما يتحقق بتعلق حقهم بما يتعلق به التصرف فيه والقصاص ليس بمال فلا يتعلق به لكنه موروث ا هـ . أقول: في تقرير البحث المذكور عفا يعتير من الثلث الخطأ لأن في أن
Page 05, Book of offences, chapter of retaliation for less than life, even with its absolute wording is the saying of the Imam. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A man cut another man's hand unjustly intentionally, and the amputee forgave the cutting, then it spread to the soul and he died; or he gashed a man's head intentionally, and the gashed forgave the gash, then it spread to the soul and he died. It must be known that there are two issues: one in intentional and the other in mistake. Each issue has aspects: either the amputee says 'I forgive you the injury' or says 'I forgive you the cutting and what results from it'. If the injury was intentional and the amputee or the gashed said 'I forgive you the injury', the forgiveness is valid and he is cleared from the cutting or gash, or if he dies nothing is due in both cases, then clearance from all wealth is valid, whether he recovers or dies. And if he said 'I forgive you the cutting' and did not say 'and what results from the cutting', or said 'I forgive you the gash' and did not say 'and what results from it', the forgiveness is valid according to all of them, but if he dies, diyah is obligatory. Abu Hanifa said: although the forgiveness is void, and retaliation is obligatory on the one forgiven, except that I deem it good (istihsan) that diyah is obligatory from his wealth. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: the forgiveness is valid and there is nothing on the one forgiven, neither retaliation nor diyah. And this which we mentioned is when the injury was intentional. If it was mistaken, if he forgives the injury or the cutting and what results from it, the forgiveness is valid whether he recovers or dies, except that if he forgives at a time when he goes out and comes and goes after the injury, according to some mashayikh it is considered from all his wealth. And it is mentioned in al-Muntaqa in this case that it is considered from one-third of the wealth. And if he forgives the cutting, confining to the cutting, if he recovers, the forgiveness is valid without dispute from all his wealth, and if he becomes a killer, then according to Abu Hanifa the forgiveness is void and the diyah is on the 'aqila of the killer; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the forgiveness is valid as if he forgave the cutting and what results from it, except that in a state of health, i.e., he goes and comes, it is valid from all his wealth, and analogically to the narration of al-Muntaqa from one-third of his wealth; if he forgives in a state of illness, i.e., he becomes bedridden, it is considered from one-third of his wealth. And if he said 'I forgive the injury' or 'I forgive the cutter and what results from it', it is forgiveness regarding the diyah of the soul by consensus, such that if he dies, the entire diyah is dropped. However, its cause is wealth, and the right of heirs is attached to it, so it is considered from one-third like other wealth, contrary to intentional injury, where the cause is retaliation and no right of heirs attaches because it is not wealth. Al-'Inaya said: There is a discussion: retaliation is inherited by consensus, so how does the right of heirs not attach? Then he said: The answer is that the author negated the attachment of the heirs' right to it, not that it is not inherited. There is no contradiction because the heirs' right is established by way of succession, and the ruling of the successor is not established with the existence of the original. Likewise, analogically in wealth, the attachment of the heirs' right should not be established except after the death of the testator, but it is established legally by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed, to leave your heirs rich is better than to leave them poor, begging from people.' And leaving them rich is only realized by attaching their right to that which disposition is possible in, and retaliation is not wealth, so it does not attach, but it is inherited. End. I say: in the exposition of the aforementioned discussion, forgiveness is considered from one-third in mistake because in that...
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, commenting on a quote from al-Jami' al-Saghir. It addresses the effect of a victim's forgiveness of an injury (like amputation) when the injury later proves fatal. The main issue is: if the victim forgives only the act of cutting (al-qat') without mentioning its consequences, and then dies from the injury, does diyah become due? The passage first quotes a scenario from al-Jami' al-Saghir: a person intentionally cuts off another's hand or inflicts a head wound, then the victim forgives the cutting or the gash, and the injury leads to death. The ruling depends on the wording of forgiveness. If the victim said 'I forgive the injury' (al-jinaayah), the forgiveness is valid and the culprit is free from both retaliation and diyah. If the victim said 'I forgive the cutting' specifically, then according to all scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), the forgiveness is valid regarding the physical act, but if he dies, diyah is due. However, Abu Hanifa considers the forgiveness of the cutting void because it was not comprehensive, and he applies istihsan to require diyah from the culprit's wealth. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider the forgiveness valid even if limited, so no diyah. The passage then distinguishes between intentional and accidental injuries. In accidental injuries, forgiveness of either the injury or the cutting (with consequences) is valid, but the financial implications depend on whether the victim was in health or illness at the time of forgiveness: if healthy, the forgiveness is effective from all his wealth; if ill, it is limited to one-third, as per the view in al-Muntaqa. The passage ends with a discussion from al-'Inaya about why the heirs' right does not attach to qisas even though it is inherited: because qisas is not wealth, so the heirs' right only attaches after the death of the testator but qisas is not transferable property, though it is inherited as a right.

Key Terms
العفو (al-Afw): The victim's forgiveness of the injury or its consequences, which can waive qisas and/or diyah depending on wording and circumstances.
السراية (al-Siraayah): The spread of an injury from the initial wound to the whole body, causing death.
الثلث (al-Thuluth): One-third of the wealth, which is the maximum a person may bequeath or give away in illness, and the limit for forgiveness that is effective from the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when the victim says 'I forgive you the cutting' and nothing more, and then dies, what is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?
A) The forgiveness is void and diyah is due.
B) The forgiveness is valid and no diyah is due.
C) The forgiveness is void but diyah is not due.
D) The forgiveness is valid but only half of the diyah is due.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on the effect of limited forgiveness: Abu Hanifa requires diyah by istihsan, but the relied-upon view (Sahibayn) holds the forgiveness valid and no diyah due.

Representation of Absent Heir in Homicide: Intentional vs Unintentional
Ruling on representation in homicide testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on representation of an absent heir in homicide cases and explain the distinction between intentional and unintentional killing, including the intra-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
In homicide, the present heir represents the absent only for intentional killing — unintentional requires each heir's independent claim.

This passage addresses a procedural question: when one heir is present and another is absent, can the present heir act as a legal opponent (khusuma) for the absent in matters of proving the killing or accepting a pardon? The answer depends crucially on whether the killing was intentional or unintentional, and there is a well-known disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. This lesson will guide you through the rule, its evidence, and the practical outcome of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is 'khusuma' (legal representation) by a present heir for an absent heir in homicide-related testimony. The ruling: for intentional killing, the present heir can represent the absent in proving the killing and accepting pardon. For unintentional killing, representation is not allowed (by the majority position).
The passage also discusses a parallel case of jointly owned slaves.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) from the case of debt: one creditor can represent others in proving a debt. Similarly, in intentional killing, the blood-money (or qisas) is a single demand, so one heir can act for all.
The analogy is khafi (subtle) because homicide involves physical harm, not just financial claims.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is that the claim is unified: in intentional killing, the right to qisas or blood-money is shared; proving it benefits all heirs. In unintentional killing, each heir's right to blood-money is independent, so representation is not automatic.
Abu Hanifa extends the analogy to unintentional, arguing the claim is still financial and can be proven collectively.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that one heir can represent the absent even in unintentional killing. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree, restricting representation to intentional killing only.
Their evidence is that each heir's share in unintentional blood-money is a separate entitlement, unlike the unified claim in intentional.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: no representation in unintentional killing. This is the view adopted in Zahir al-Riwayah and by later authorities like al-Marghinani.
The practical consequence: in unintentional killing, the absent heir must be present or appoint a representative; otherwise, the present heir can only claim his own share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو خطأ أو ديناً لا فإن أثبت القاتل عفو الغائب لم يعد وكذا لو قتل عبدهما وأحدهما غائب وإن شهد وليان بعفو ثالثهما لغت فإن صدقهما القاتل فالدية لهم اثلاثاً وإن كذبهما فلا شيء لهما وللآخر ثلث الدية وأن أشهدا أنه ضربه فلم يزل صاحب فراش تزوجتك على ألف درهم فقبلت فهو نكاح فكان المراد منه الإيجاب فكذا هذا. قال رحمه الله : ( وكذا لو قتل عبدهما وأحدهما غائب) أي لو كان عبد بين رجلين فقتل عمداً وأحد الموليين غائب فحكمه مثل ما ذكرنا أحد في الوليين حتى يقتل بينة أقامها الحاضر من غير إعادة بعد عود الغائب، ولو أقام القاتل البينة أن الغائب قد عفا فالشاهد خصم ويسقط القصاص لما بينا فحاصله أن هذه المسألة مثل الأولى في جميع ما ذكرنا إلا أنه إذا كان القتل عمداً أو خطأ لا يكون الحاضر خصماً الغائب بالإجماع والفرق لهما في الكل. ولأبي حنيفة في الخطأ. أن أحد الورثة خصم عن الباقين على ما بينا ولا كذلك أحد الموليين على ما عرف في موضعه وقدمنا له مزيد بيان عند ذكر الكبير والصغير فارجع إليه .
And if [the killing was] unintentional or a debt, no. If the killer establishes the absent's pardon, it does not need to be repeated. Similarly, if the slave of both is killed and one of them is absent. And if two guardians testify about the pardon of a third, it is invalid. If the killer confirms them, the blood-money is for them in thirds. And if he denies them, then nothing for them, and for the other is one-third of the blood-money. And if they testify that he struck him and he did not cease to be the occupant of the bed... You married me for one thousand dirhams and he accepted, so it is marriage, so the meaning was offer, likewise here. He (the author) said: (Similarly, if the slave of both is killed and one of them is absent) meaning: if a slave is jointly owned by two men and is killed intentionally, and one of the owners is absent, then its ruling is like what we mentioned for one of the two guardians, until he completes the evidence presented by the present one without repetition after the absent returns. And if the killer presents evidence that the absent one has pardoned, then the witness is an opponent and qisas is dropped for the reason we mentioned. So the gist is that this case is like the first in all we mentioned, except that if the killing is intentional or unintentional, the present one is not an opponent for the absent by consensus, and there is a difference between them in all. And for Abu Hanifa on unintentional: that one of the heirs is an opponent over the rest as we said, and not so for one of the two owners, as known in its place. And we have given further explanation when discussing the major and minor, so refer back to it.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about representation (khusuma) of an absent heir in homicide cases. The author explains that if a slave owned by two is killed intentionally and one owner is absent, the present owner can establish the killing by testimony and the absent owner is bound by the judgment, just as in the case of two guardians. However, if the killer brings proof that the absent owner has pardoned, the present owner then becomes an opponent and qisas is dropped. The key point is the distinction between intentional and unintentional killing: the present owner cannot represent the absent in unintentional killing by consensus, but Abu Hanifa holds that in unintentional killing, one heir can represent the others. This is because in unintentional killing, the blood-money is divided among heirs, and each has an independent claim, so representation is not automatic. The author notes this has been explained previously.

Key Terms
خصومة (khusuma): Legal representation in a lawsuit where one party acts as opponent on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a jointly owned slave killed intentionally, can the present owner represent the absent owner in proving the killing?
A) Yes, in both intentional and unintentional killing.
B) Yes, only in intentional killing.
C) No, not at all.
D) Only if the absent owner agrees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the right to represent an absent heir in homicide depends on the type of killing: representation is allowed for intentional killing but not for unintentional, with Abu Hanifa differing on the latter.

Testimony of Two Heirs about a Third's Pardon
Ruling on the invalidity of testimony by two heirs that a third heir has pardoned the killer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony by two heirs about a third's pardon and explain why it is invalid due to drawing personal benefit.

Core Idea
Testimony that brings a financial benefit to the witness is invalid in Hanafi law.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Hanafi fiqh: when two heirs testify that a third heir has pardoned the killer in a homicide case, their testimony is generally invalid. The reason is that the witnesses stand to benefit by converting the right of qisas (retaliation) into blood-money (diyah), thereby increasing their own shares. However, an exception exists in unintentional killing if the witnesses have not yet taken their shares of blood-money. This ruling is based on the fundamental principle that testimony must be free from any personal interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the specific act: two heirs testify that a third heir has pardoned the killer. The ruling is that such testimony is invalid (batil) in intentional killing.
The ruling may differ in unintentional killing, as noted in al-Muhit.
2
Understand the rationale (talil)
The rationale is that the witnesses draw benefit to themselves (jarr al-naf'). By testifying that the third pardoned, the right of qisas is converted into diyah, which the witnesses then share. Their testimony thus brings them financial gain, tainting their impartiality.
This is a key principle in Hanafi law: testimony that benefits the witness is rejected.
3
Note the exception in unintentional killing
According to al-Muhit, in unintentional killing, if the two witnesses have not yet taken their shares of diyah, their testimony about the third's pardon is valid. The reason is that they do not benefit from the testimony because the diyah is not yet divided.
If they have already taken their shares, the testimony becomes beneficial and thus invalid.
4
Recognize the analogous debt case
The text from al-Mabsut analogizes: if three creditors are owed a debt, and two testify that the third discharged his share, their testimony is invalid because it benefits them by increasing their share of the remaining debt.
The analogy reinforces the same principle: benefit invalidates testimony.
5
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Now that you understand the principle, you can apply it to other cases where a witness might benefit. Ask: does this testimony bring a direct or indirect benefit to the witness? If yes, the testimony is invalid per Hanafi law.
This is a common reasoning tool in fiqh al-shahadat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وإن شهد وليان بعفو ثالثهما لغت ) أي إذا كان أولياء المقتول ثلاثة فشهد اثنان منهم على الثالث أنه عفا فشهادتهما باطلة لأنهما يجران لأنفسهما نفعاً انقلاب القود وهو مالاً وهو عفو منهما وزعمهما معتبر في حق أنفسهما إطلاق في قوله بعفو ثالثهما فشمل ما إذا كان في العمد والخطأ. وقيد في المحيط الخطأ حيث قال: فشهادتهما جائزة في الخطأ إذا لم يقبضا نصيبهما ا.هـ. وإنما قيد به لأنهما إذا قبضا نصيبهم لم يحتاجا إلى إثبات عفو الغائب لأن العفو حصل منهما وهو قيد حسن لا بد منه، ولو قيد به المؤلف لكان أولى. وذكر في المبسوط في كتاب الصلح : والمأذون في دين بين ثلاثة شهد اثنان على الثالث أنه أبرأ عن نصيبه لا تقبل لأن شهادتهما تجر لأنفسهما نفعاً لأن شهادتهما تقطع شركة المشهود عليه في الباقي من الدين فلا تقبل كما لو شهد أنه أبرأه عن نصيبه بعد ما قبضا نصيبهما.
He (the author) said: (And if two guardians testify about the pardon of a third, it is invalid) meaning: if the guardians of the slain are three, and two of them testify against the third that he pardoned, their testimony is invalid because they draw benefit to themselves: the conversion of qisas into wealth, and it is a pardon from them, and their claim is considered valid regarding themselves. The expression 'about the pardon of a third' is general and includes intentional and unintentional killing. In al-Muhit it is restricted to unintentional where it says: their testimony is permissible in unintentional if they have not taken their shares. He restricted it because if they have taken their shares, they do not need to prove the absent's pardon, since the pardon came from them. This is a good necessary restriction; if the author had included it, it would be better. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut in the Book of Compromise: regarding a debt among three, if two testify that the third has discharged his share, it is not accepted because their testimony draws benefit to themselves: their testimony cuts off the partnership of the testifiee in the remainder of the debt, so it is not accepted, just as if they testified that he discharged him after they had taken their shares.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the invalidity of testimony by two heirs about the third's pardon. The author states the general rule: such testimony is invalid because the witnesses benefit from it – by testifying that the third pardoned, they convert the right of qisas into blood-money for themselves. Their claim of the third's pardon is essentially their own pardon which they assert. However, a condition is mentioned from al-Muhit: in unintentional killing, if the witnesses have not yet taken their shares of blood-money, their testimony is valid because they do not benefit from it (since the blood-money is not yet divided). The author critiques that the author of al-Kanz did not include this condition. Then he analogizes to a debt case from al-Mabsut: if three creditors and two testify that the third discharged his share, it is rejected because it benefits them (they get a larger share of the remaining debt). The principle is: testimony that benefits the witness is invalid.

Key Terms
جر النفع (jarr al-naf'): Drawing benefit to oneself through testimony, which renders the testimony invalid.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court.
ولي (wali): Guardian or heir of the victim in homicide cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the third heir is absent.
B) Because the witnesses draw benefit to themselves by converting qisas into blood-money.
C) Because the killer objects.
D) Because the pardon was not in writing.

Key Takeaway
Testimony that draws a personal benefit to the witness is invalid in Hanafi fiqh, with an exception in unintentional killing if the witnesses have not yet taken their shares of diyah.

Testimony of Deferring Killing for a Fee
Ruling on testimony that the heir deferred the killing till evening for a fixed fee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a mere deferral of qisas and a conditional pardon for a fee, and state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of the fee in each case.

Core Idea
A fee for merely deferring qisas is invalid; only a pardon in exchange for compensation is valid, and time limits in pardons are void.

This passage examines two scenarios involving a blood-warden (walī al-dam) who delays the killer's execution in exchange for a fee. The key legal question is whether such a delay constitutes a valid compromise (sulh) that cancels qisas, or whether the fee is simply void. The author explains the distinction between a bare deferral and a conditional pardon, using qiyas (analogy) to similar rulings in divorce and emancipation. By the end, you will understand when such agreements are valid and when they are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the two distinct situations: (1) the heir defers the killing 'till night for a known fee' without explicit pardon; (2) the heir takes the fee 'on condition that he pardon him for one day'. These yield different rulings.
The first scenario involves only delay; the second involves a conditional pardon.
2
Apply the ruling on deferral
The author states that deferring a right does not cancel it; thus postponing execution does not waive qisas. The fee is invalid because it is compensation for time, which is not a valid consideration (ja'l). Underline the principle: time cannot be a countervalue.
This is a general Hanafi rule: al-ījār 'alā al-zamān bāṭil.
3
Analyze the conditional pardon scenario
When the heir explicitly says 'I pardon him for one day' in exchange for the fee, this is a valid compromise (sulh). The pardon is effective but the time limitation is void, because pardon does not accept time restriction. The fee is valid as compensation for the pardon itself.
The time limit is canceled, so the pardon is immediate and unconditional.
4
Understand the qiyas to divorce and emancipation
The author draws an analogy: if a man divorces his wife or emancipates his slave for a fee payable by a deadline, the divorce/emancipation is valid and the fee is due, but the deadline is void. Similarly, the pardon with a time limit is valid, the time limit is void, and the fee is owed.
The common illa (effective cause) is that a condition of time in a contract that does not accept time limitation renders the condition void but the contract valid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position as stated by al-Marghinani is that mere deferral is not a pardon and the fee is invalid; but a conditional pardon valid. This is the relied-upon ruling for fatwa.
Other schools may differ; al-Marghinani's authority is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شهد شاهدان على ولي الدم أنه أخر القاتل اليوم إلى الليل على جعل معلوم لم يكن عفواً ولا مال له لأن تأخير الحق يقتضي سقوطه فكذا تأجيل القتل لا يقتضي سقوطه والمال باطل لأنه لو وجب عوضاً عن الأجل والاعتياض عن الأجل باطل ولو شهد على أنه أخذ الجعل على أن يعفو عنه يوماً كان صلحاً لأنه عفا عن القصاص يوماً والعفو لا يقبل التأقيت فصح العفو وبطل التأقيت، وصار كما لو طلق امرأته وأعتق عبده على ألف إلى الليل جاز الصلح وبطل التأقيت فكذا هذا. وقوله «على أن يعفو ولم يخرج مخرج العدة وإنما يراد به الإخبار كالرجل يقول للمرأة تزوجتك على ألف درهم فقبلت فهو نكاح فكان المراد منه الإيجاب فكذا هذا.
Two witnesses testified against the blood-warden that he deferred the killer from today till night for a known fee. This is not considered a pardon, nor does he get the money, because deferring a right does not entail its dropping; similarly, postponing killing does not entail its dropping. The money is void because if it were compensation for the deferment, compensation for time is void. If they testify that he took the fee on condition that he pardon him for one day, then it is a compromise (sulh), because he pardoned qisas for one day, and pardon does not accept time limitation, so the pardon is valid and the time limitation is void. It becomes as if he divorced his wife and emancipated his slave for one thousand [dirhams] until night: the compromise is valid and the time limitation is void. Similarly here. And his saying 'on condition that he pardon' is not an oath but is meant as declaration, like a man saying to a woman 'I marry you for one thousand dirhams' and she accepts, that is marriage, so the meaning is offer; likewise here.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about testimony that the heir deferred the killer's execution till evening for a fee. The author explains that such deferral does not amount to a pardon of qisas, nor does the heir deserve the fee, because deferring a right does not cancel it. However, if the heir explicitly said 'I pardon him for one day' in exchange for the fee, then it is a valid compromise (sulh): the pardon is effective but the time limitation is void. The analogy is given: if a man says to his wife 'You are divorced on condition you pay me 1000 dirhams by night' and she accepts, the divorce is valid and the condition is void; similarly, if one emancipates his slave for money by a deadline, the emancipation is valid and the deadline void. The phrase 'on condition that he pardon' is treated as an offer, not an oath, analogous to marriage proposal and acceptance.

Key Terms
جعل (ja'l): A fee or compensation given for a service or benefit.
صلح (sulh): A compromise settling a dispute; here used to replace qisas with monetary compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a blood-warden takes a fee on condition that he pardons the killer for one day?
A) Both the pardon and the time limit are valid.
B) The pardon is valid, but the time limit is void, and the fee is owed.
C) The pardon is void because it is time-limited, so the fee is invalid.
D) The entire agreement is void because it involves a fee for delay.

Key Takeaway
A fee for merely deferring qisas is invalid; only a pardon in exchange for compensation is valid, but any time limit in the pardon is void.

Killer's Confirmation or Denial of Witnesses: Blood-Money Distribution
Ruling on blood-money distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the killer's confirmation or denial of witnesses' testimony determines blood-money distribution and explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
The killer's admission or denial of witnesses' testimony determines blood-money distribution, overriding qiyas by istihsan.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi ruling on blood-money (diyah) when two heirs testify that a third heir pardoned the killer from qisas. The killer's response—confirmation or denial—drastically changes liability. The author presents the rule, then justifies it with istihsan over the qiyas that would otherwise exonerate the killer. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school uses istihsan to achieve just outcomes in complex inheritance and homicide cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenarios
The passage describes two main scenarios: (1) the killer confirms the witnesses, meaning he admits they are truthful; (2) the killer denies them, along with the third heir's denial of pardoning. Understand the legal outcomes for each.
The third heir is the one alleged to have pardoned.
2
Analyze the Legal Effect
When the killer confirms, he admits two-thirds of the blood-money to the witnesses, and the third heir (denying pardon) gets one-third. When he denies, the witnesses lose their claim, but the third heir gets one-third from the killer because the witnesses' testimony is treated as their admission of pardon for him.
The third heir's right arises from the witnesses' own admission, not from his claim.
3
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
There is disagreement on the recipient of the one-third when the killer confirms: al-Jami' as-Saghir says it goes to the witnesses; other works say to the testifiee. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that it goes to the witnesses, as al-Marghinani adopts.
This dispute is resolved by tarjih favoring the witnesses.
4
Understand the Istihsan Argument
The qiyas would be that the killer owes nothing because the witnesses' claim is unproven (due to his denial) and his admission to the testifiee is nullified by the testifiee's claim of pardon. But istihsan gives effect to the killer's admission, analogizing to a debtor who admits a debt but the creditor redirects it to another.
Istihsan prevents injustice by upholding the binding nature of admissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن صدقهما القاتل فالدية لهم اثلاثاً أي صدقهما القاتل دون الولي المشهود عليه لأن تصديقه لهما إقرار لهما بثلثي الدية ويلزمه لأنهم كانوا يزعمون أن نصيب الولي المشهود عليه قد سقط بعفوه وهو ينكر فلا يقبل قولهم عليه فوجب عليه كل الدية وللمنكر ثلثها. قال رحمه الله : (وإن كذبهما فلا شيء لهما وللآخر ثلث الدية أي إن كذبهما القاتل أيضاً بعد أن كذبهما الولي المشهود عليه بالعفو فلا شيء للوليين الشاهدين لأن شهادتهما عليه إقرار ببطلان حقهما عليه في القصاص فصح إقرارهما في حق أنفسهما، وإن ادعيا انقلابهما مالاً فلا يصدقا في دعواهما إلا ببينة وللولي المشهود عليه ثلث الدية لأن شهادتهما عليه بالعفو وهو ينكر بمنزلة إقرارهما بالعفو فينقلب نصيبهما مالاً وفي النهاية : وإن كذبهما المشهود عليه يجب على القاتل دية كاملة بينهم اثلاثاً فجعل الضمير فاعل كذبهما المشهود عليه لا القاتل. قال الشارح : وإن صدقهما الولي المشهود عليه وحده دون القاتل ضمن القاتل ثلث الدية للولي المشهود عليه لأنه أقر له بذلك فإن قيل : كيف له الثلث وهو قد أقر أنه لا يستحق على القاتل شيئاً بدعواه العفو؟ قلنا : ارتد إقراره بتكذيب القاتل إياه فوجب له ثلث الدية عليه. وفي الجامع الصغير كان هذا الثلث للشاهدين لا للمشهود عليه وهو الأصح لأن المشهود عليه يزعم أنه قد عفا أو لا شيء له وللشاهدين على القاتل ثلث الدية ديناً . ذمته في والذي في يده وهو ثلث الدية مال القاتل وهو من جنس حقهما فيصرف إليهما لإقراره لهما بذلك كمن قال لفلان علي ألف درهم فقال المقر له ليس ذلك لي وإنما هو لفلان فإنه يصرف إليه فكذا هنا، وهذا كله استحسان. والقياس أن لا يلزم القاتل شيء لأن ما ادعاه الشاهدان على القاتل لم يثبت لإنكاره وما أقر به القاتل للمشهود عليه قد بطل بإقراره بالعفو لكونه تكذيباً له. وجوابه أن القائل بتكذيب الشاهدين قد أقر للمشهود عليه بثلث الدية لزعمه أن القصاص قد سقط بشهادتهما كما إذا عفا والمقر له لم يكذب القاتل حقيقة بل أضاف الوجوب إلى غيره فجعل الواجب للشاهدين وفي مثله لا يرتد الإقرار كمن قال لفلان علي كذا فقال المقر له ليس لي ولكنه لفلان على ما بينا قيد المؤلف بقوله ولو شهد اثنان وإن كان الحكم في الواحد كذلك لأنه إذا علم أن شهادة الاثنين باطلة علم ببطلان شهادة الواحد الفرد من باب أولى.
He (the author) said: (If the killer confirms them, then the blood-money is for them in thirds) meaning: the killer confirms them apart from the testifiee guardian, because his confirmation of them is an admission to them of two-thirds of the blood-money, and it becomes obligatory upon him. Since they claimed that the share of the testifiee guardian had dropped due to his pardon, and he denies, their statement is not accepted against him, so he owes the entire blood-money, and the denier gets one-third. He (the author) said: (And if he denies them, then nothing for them, and for the other is one-third of the blood-money) meaning: if the killer also denies them after the testifiee guardian denied their testimony about the pardon, then nothing for the two witnesses, because their testimony against him is an admission of the invalidity of their right against him in qisas, so their admission is valid regarding themselves. And if they claim that it converts to wealth, they are not believed without evidence. And for the testifiee guardian is one-third of the blood-money, because their testimony about the pardon while he denies is like their admission of the pardon, so their share converts to wealth. In an-Nihayah: if the testifiee denies them, the killer owes a complete blood-money divided among them in thirds, making the subject of 'denies' the testifiee, not the killer. The commentator said: If the testifiee guardian alone confirms them without the killer, the killer owes one-third of the blood-money to the testifiee guardian because he admitted that to him. If it is said: how can he get the third when he admitted that he deserves nothing from the killer due to his claim of pardon? We say: his admission is overturned by the killer's denial of him, so one-third of the blood-money is due from the killer. In al-Jami' as-Saghir, this third is for the witnesses, not the testifiee, and it is the most correct, because the testifiee claims he has pardoned or nothing is due, and for the witnesses against the killer is one-third of the blood-money as a debt in his liability. What is in his hand is one-third of the blood-money of the killer, and it is of the same type as their right, so it is given to them due to his admission to them. Like one who says: 'I owe so-and-so a thousand dirhams,' and the say-so-and-so says: 'That is not mine, it is for so-and-so,' then it is given to the latter. Likewise here. All this is istihsan. The qiyas would be that nothing is owed by the killer, because what the witnesses claimed against the killer is not established due to his denial, and what the killer admitted to the testifiee is nullified by his admission of pardon as a denial of him. The answer: the one who denies the witnesses has admitted to the testifiee one-third of the blood-money due to his claim that qisas fell by their testimony, as if he pardoned. And the admittee did not actually deny the killer but attributed the obligation to someone else, making the due for the witnesses. In such a case, the admission is not overturned, as in the example above. The author's restriction 'if two witness' even though the ruling for one is similar, because when it is known that the testimony of two is invalid, it is known that the testimony of one individual is invalid a fortiori.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing the consequences when two heirs testify about a third's pardon. The author explains two scenarios: if the killer confirms the witnesses, then he owes the full blood-money, with the denying heir receiving one-third and the witnesses two-thirds. If the killer and the testifiee both deny, the witnesses get nothing and the testifiee gets one-third from the killer. There is also a discussion of cases where only the testifiee confirms, or only the killer denies. The author notes that according to al-Jami' as-Saghir, the one-third is given to the witnesses, not the testifiee, citing istihsan. The qiyas would lead to no liability for the killer, but istihsan operates to give effect to the killer's admission. The passage also notes that the same ruling applies to a single witness by analogy.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a more equitable outcome.
دية (diyah): Blood-money, monetary compensation paid to the heirs of a homicide victim in lieu of qisas.
قود (qisas): Retributive justice, right of the victim's heirs to demand the death penalty or pardon.
إقرار (iqrar): Admission or confession, a binding declaration against oneself.

Key Takeaway
The killer's admission or denial of witnesses' testimony determines blood-money distribution, with istihsan ensuring liability despite qiyas to the contrary.

Parsing the Five Scenarios of Heir Testimony on Pardon
Classification of testimony scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two main divisions and list the five aspects of the first division when one heir testifies against the other about pardon.

Core Idea
One heir's testimony about the other's pardon splits into five distinct cases based on who confirms or denies.

This passage from al-Mabsut provides a systematic classification of a specific evidentiary problem: when one heir (wali) testifies that the other heir has pardoned the killer regarding qisas or blood-money. The text establishes two overarching divisions and then begins to detail the first division, which has five possibilities depending on the reactions of the companion heir and the killer. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for correctly evaluating the legal effect of such testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main divisions
The text says the case is divided into two parts: either one heir testifies against the other about pardon, or each testifies against the other. Understand these as distinct scenarios.
The first division is the focus of the given text.
2
Enumerate the five aspects of the first division
The text begins listing the five possibilities for the case where one heir testifies. They are based on whether the companion (the accused heir) and the killer confirm or deny the testimony.
Only the first two aspects are fully given: both confirm, both deny. The rest are implied.
3
Determine the missing aspects
From the pattern, the other three aspects likely involve mixed confirmations: companion denies and killer confirms, companion confirms and killer denies, and perhaps one of them remains silent or gives a different response.
Use your knowledge of fiqh to complete the set logically.
4
Associate each aspect with its likely ruling
Although the ruling is not stated here, in Hanafi fiqh the testimony of one heir against the other may be accepted or rejected based on the degree of confirmation. For example, if both confirm, the testimony is established; if both deny, it is not.
This step prepares you for the next lesson that will discuss the rulings.

Ruling on Testimony of Two Witnesses Regarding 'Afw and Diyah Distribution
Explanation of the ruling when killer confirms or denies witnesses' claim of 'afw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah distribution when two witnesses testify about 'afw, identify the two scenarios (killer confirms vs denies), and explain the preferred view within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
When the killer denies the witnesses, they lose their share; the disputed third goes to the witnesses, per al-Jami' al-Saghir.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on a nuanced scenario in the law of qisas. Two witnesses, who are also guardians, testify that a third guardian has waived his right to retaliation. The commentary explores what happens when the killer confirms or denies their testimony, and an intra-Hanafi dispute over the distribution of diyah. Understanding this ruling clarifies how admissions and denials shape legal outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
Two witnesses (both guardians) testify that the third guardian waived qisas. The killer may either confirm (tasdiq) or deny (takdhib) their testimony.
The witnesses are also guardians, so their testimony affects their own rights.
2
Case 1: Killer confirms
When the killer confirms, he must pay full diyah divided equally among all three guardians because his confirmation is treated as an admission (iqrar) against himself.
The diyah is wajib on the killer; distribution is equal thirds.
3
Case 2: Killer denies
When the killer denies along with the witnessed-against guardian, the two witnesses get nothing because their testimony is an admission that their own right to qisas is extinguished. The witnessed-against guardian receives one-third because the witnesses' claim of 'afw converts his share into money.
If the witnessed-against guardian alone confirms, the killer pays him one-third (but this view is superseded).
4
Intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Jami' al-Saghir holds that the one-third should go to the witnesses, not the witnessed-against guardian. The commentator adopts this as the more correct view (al-ashah). The basis is that the guardian who claims 'afw has no right, and the killer's admission is redirected to the witnesses by istihsan.
The initial explanation from al-Nihayah gives the third to the guarded-against guardian, but the preferred view is the opposite.
5
Istihsan vs Qiyas
Strict qiyas would give nothing to anyone because the witnesses' claim is unproven and the killer's admission is nullified. However, istihsan overrides qiyas, using an analogy with a debt scenario to channel the third to the witnesses.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of preferring istihsan where qiyas leads to hardship or inconsistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن صدقهما القاتل فالدية لهم اثلاثاً) أي صدقهما القاتل دون الولي المشهود عليه لأن تصديقه لهما إقرار لهما بثلثي الدية ويلزمه لأنهم كانوا يزعمون أن نصيب الولي المشهود عليه قد سقط بعفوه وهو ينكر فلا يقبل قولهم عليه فوجب عليه كل الدية وللمنكر ثلثها. قال رحمه الله : (وإن كذبهما فلا شيء لهما وللآخر ثلث الدية) أي إن كذبهما القاتل أيضاً بعد أن كذبهما الولي المشهود عليه بالعفو فلا شيء للوليين الشاهدين لأن شهادتهما عليه إقرار ببطلان حقهما عليه في القصاص فصح إقرارهما في حق أنفسهما، وإن ادعيا انقلابهما مالاً فلا يصدقا في دعواهما إلا ببينة وللولي المشهود عليه ثلث الدية لأن شهادتهما عليه بالعفو وهو ينكر بمنزلة إقرارهما بالعفو فينقلب نصيبهما مالاً وفي النهاية : وإن كذبهما المشهود عليه يجب على القاتل دية كاملة بينهم اثلاثاً فجعل الضمير فاعل كذبهما المشهود عليه لا القاتل. قال الشارح : وإن صدقهما الولي المشهود عليه وحده دون القاتل ضمن القاتل ثلث الدية للولي المشهود عليه لأنه أقر له بذلك فإن قيل : كيف له الثلث وهو قد أقر أنه لا يستحق على القاتل شيئاً بدعواه العفو؟ قلنا : ارتد إقراره بتكذيب القاتل إياه فوجب له ثلث الدية عليه. وفي الجامع الصغير كان هذا الثلث للشاهدين لا للمشهود عليه وهو الأصح لأن المشهود عليه يزعم أنه قد عفا أو لا شيء له وللشاهدين على القاتل ثلث الدية ديناً . ذمته في والذي في يده وهو ثلث الدية مال القاتل وهو من جنس حقهما فيصرف إليهما لإقراره لهما بذلك كمن قال لفلان علي ألف درهم فقال المقر له ليس ذلك لي وإنما هو لفلان فإنه يصرف إليه فكذا هنا، وهذا كله استحسان. والقياس أن لا يلزم القاتل شيء لأن ما ادعاه الشاهدان على القاتل لم يثبت لإنكاره وما أقر به القاتل للمشهود عليه قد بطل بإقراره بالعفو لكونه تكذيباً له. وجوابه أن القائل بتكذيب الشاهدين قد أقر للمشهود عليه بثلث الدية لزعمه أن القصاص قد سقط بشهادتهما كما إذا عفا والمقر له لم يكذب القاتل حقيقة بل أضاف الوجوب إلى غيره فجعل الواجب للشاهدين وفي مثله لا يرتد الإقرار كمن قال لفلان علي كذا فقال المقر له ليس لي ولكنه لفلان على ما بينا قيد المؤلف بقوله ولو شهد اثنان وإن كان الحكم في الواحد كذلك لأنه إذا علم أن شهادة الاثنين باطلة علم ببطلان شهادة الواحد الفرد من باب أولى. ولم يتعرض لما إذا شهدا معاً أو متعاقباً ونحن نذكر ذلك ونذكر شهادة الفرد تتميماً للفائدة .
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If the killer confirms them, then the blood money is for them in thirds) meaning that the killer confirmed them but not the guardian witnessed against, because his confirmation of them is an admission for them of two-thirds of the blood money and it is binding on him, because they were claiming that the share of the guardian witnessed against had fallen due to his forgiveness, and he denies it, so their statement is not accepted against him, so the full blood money is obligatory on him, and for the denier is its third. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he denies them, then nothing is for them, and for the other is a third of the blood money) meaning that if the killer also denies them after the guardian witnessed against had denied them regarding the forgiveness, then nothing is for the two witnessing guardians, because their testimony against him is an admission of the nullity of their own right against him in retaliation, so their admission is valid regarding themselves. And if they claim that it converted into wealth, they are not believed in their claim without evidence. And for the guardian witnessed against is a third of the blood money, because their testimony against him of forgiveness while he denies it is like their admission of forgiveness, so his share converts into wealth. And in al-Nihayah: If the witnessed-against denies them, the killer must pay full blood money among them in thirds, making the pronoun subject of 'denies' the witnessed-against, not the killer. The commentator said: If the witnessed-against guardian confirms them alone without the killer, the killer is liable for a third of the blood money for the witnessed-against guardian, because he admitted that for him. If it is said: How can he have the third when he has admitted that he deserves nothing from the killer due to his claim of forgiveness? We say: His admission is refuted by the killer's denial of him, so a third of the blood money is obligatory on him (the killer) for him. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: This third is for the two witnesses, not for the witnessed-against, and it is the correct view, because the witnessed-against claims that he has forgiven, so he has nothing. And for the two witnesses is a third of the blood money from the killer as a debt in his liability, and what is in his hand is a third of the blood money of the killer, which is of the same type as their right, so it is given to them due to his admission for them of that, like someone who said to someone, 'I owe you a thousand dirhams,' and the person owed said, 'That is not for me, it is for so-and-so,' then it is given to that so-and-so. All this is istihsan. The analogy is that nothing is obligatory on the killer, because what the two witnesses claimed against the killer was not proven due to his denial, and what the killer admitted for the witnessed-against was nullified by his admission of forgiveness, being a denial of him. The answer is that the one who says that the denial of the two witnesses has admitted for the witnessed-against a third of the blood money because of his claim that retaliation has fallen due to their testimony, like when one forgives, and the one owed did not actually deny the killer, but rather attributed the obligation to another, making what is obligatory for the two witnesses. In such a case, the admission is not refuted, like someone who said to so-and-so, 'I owe you such-and-such,' and the person owed said, 'It is not for me, but it is for so-and-so,' as we explained. The author restricted by his saying 'even if two witnesses testify,' even though the ruling for one witness is the same, because if it is known that the testimony of two is invalid, it is known that the testimony of a single individual is invalid a fortiori. And he did not address the case if they testify together or consecutively, and we will mention that and mention the testimony of an individual to complete the benefit.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It deals with a specific scenario in the chapter of testimony in homicide: two witnesses (who are also guardians of the victim) testify that a third guardian has waived qisas (retaliation) against the killer. The commentary explains two main cases. First, if the killer confirms their testimony, he must pay full diyah (blood money) divided equally among the three guardians. The killer's confirmation is treated as an admission against himself. Second, if the killer denies their testimony along with the witnessed-against guardian's denial, the two witnesses lose their claim to any share because their testimony amounts to an admission that their own right to qisas is extinguished. However, the witnessed-against guardian receives one-third of the diyah because the witnesses' claim of 'afw against his denial converts his share into money. The commentator then notes a variant from al-Nihayah where the pronoun refers to the witnessed-against guardian. He also cites al-Jami' al-Saghir, which holds that the one-third should go to the witnesses, not the witnessed-against guardian, and this is the preferred view (al-ashah). The istihsan basis is explained: the killer's admission for the witnessed-against is redirected to the witnesses through an analogy with a debt scenario. The qiyas (strict analogy) would give nothing, but istihsan (juristic preference) prevails. The author concludes by noting that the matn only discusses two witnesses, but the same rule applies to one witness a fortiori.

Key Terms
تصديق (tasdiq): Confirmation by the killer of the witnesses' testimony
تكذيب (takdhib): Denial by the killer or the guardian of the witnesses' testimony
عفو (afw): Waiver of qisas (retaliation) by the guardian
دية (diyah): Blood money payable to the heirs of a homicide victim
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation, the right to take life in return for murder

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the killer confirms the testimony of two witnesses claiming 'afw by the third guardian, how is the diyah distributed?
A) All diyah goes to the two witnesses
B) All diyah goes to the witnessed-against guardian
C) Diyah is divided equally among all three guardians
D) The killer pays nothing

Key Takeaway
When two witnesses testify that a guardian has waived qisas, the killer's confirmation or denial determines diyah distribution, and within the Hanafi school, the preferred view gives the disputed third to the witnesses.
